<details>
<summary>Tool · 2026-03-25 02:13:18 UTC · `exec_command` `/usr/bin/zsh -lc "sed -n '1,240p' tools/lockdep/README.md"`</summary>

- Time: `2026-03-25 02:13:18 UTC`
- Exit code: `0`

```text
# cargo-lockdep

`cargo-lockdep` is a prototype static lock dependency analyzer for Asterinas.

It is currently implemented as an independent tool crate under
[tools/lockdep](/root/asterinas-codex/tools/lockdep).

The tool can be invoked directly, and it is also wired into OSDK as
`cargo osdk lockdep`.

Direct entrypoint:

```bash
cargo run --manifest-path tools/lockdep/Cargo.toml -- --help
```

OSDK entrypoint:

```bash
cargo osdk lockdep --help
```

## What It Does

... [truncated]
```

</details>

- Exit code: `0`

```text
// SPDX-License-Identifier: MPL-2.0

//! Front-end entry for the standalone static lockdep analyzer.
//!
//! This binary is responsible for:
//!
//! - parsing user-facing CLI arguments;
//! - invoking Cargo with the lockdep rustc wrapper;
//! - collecting per-crate analysis artifacts;
//! - aggregating those artifacts into global graph reports;
//! - rendering JSON, DOT, and terminal summaries.

#![feature(rustc_private)]

extern crate rustc_driver;

use std::{
    collections::{BTreeMap, BTreeSet, VecDeque},
    env,
    ffi::OsString,
    fs, io,
    path::{Path, PathBuf},
    process::{self, Command},
    time::{SystemTime, UNIX_EPOCH},
... [truncated]
```

</details>

fn normalize_args(args: impl IntoIterator<Item = OsString>) -> Vec<OsString> {
    let mut normalized = Vec::new();

    for (index, argument) in args.into_iter().enumerate() {
        if index == 1 && argument == "lockdep" {
            continue;
        }
        normalized.push(argument);
    }

    normalized
}

fn run(args: Vec<OsString>) -> Result<(), Box<dyn std::error::Error>> {
    let cli = Cli::parse_from(args);
    let manifest_path = canonicalize_manifest_path(&cli.manifest_path)?;
    let workspace_root = manifest_path
        .parent()
        .ok_or_else(|| io::Error::other("manifest path has no parent directory"))?
... [truncated]
```

    89	/// Moves the children of `current_process` to be the children of `reaper_process`.
    90	///
    91	/// If the `reaper_process` is zombie, returns `Err(())`.
    92	fn move_process_children(
    93	    current_process: &Process,
    94	    reaper_process: &Arc<Process>,
    95	) -> core::result::Result<(), ()> {
    96	    // Lock order: children of process -> parent of process
    97	    let mut reaper_process_children = reaper_process.children().lock();
    98	    let Some(reaper_process_children) = reaper_process_children.as_mut() else {
    99	        // The reaper process has exited, and it is not the init process
   100	        // (since we never clear the init process's children).
   101	        return Err(());
   102	    };

   378	    /// This method will return `EPERM` if an existing process group has the same identifier as the
   379	    /// process ID. This means that the process is or was a process group leader and that the
   380	    /// process group is still alive.

     1	// SPDX-License-Identifier: MPL-2.0
     2	
     3	//! Implements the cgroup nodes for the unified cgroup hierarchy (cgroup v2).
     4	//!
     5	//! This module defines the structures for cgroup nodes ([`CgroupNode`]) and the cgroup
     6	//! root ([`CgroupSystem`]), integrating them into the `systree`. It handles process
     7	//! management within cgroups and the logic for reading and writing cgroup attributes.
     8	//!
     9	//! ## Locks and Lock Ordering
    10	//!
    11	//! To ensure thread safety during concurrent operations, this module uses several
    12	//! locks within the cgroup nodes. Adhering to the correct lock ordering is crucial
    13	//! to prevent deadlocks.
    14	//!
    15	//! ### Lock Types
    16	//!
    17	//! 1. **Inner Lock**: Each non-root [`CgroupNode`] has an `RwMutex` that protects its
    18	//!    `inner` data.
    19	//!
    20	//! 2. **Children Lock**: Each cgroup node ([`CgroupNode`] and [`CgroupSystem`]) inherits
    21	//!    an `RwMutex` from `BranchNodeFields`. This lock protects access to and
    22	//!    modification of the list of child cgroup nodes.
    23	//!
    24	//! 3. **Cgroup Membership Lock**: A global `RwMutex` managed by [`CgroupMembership`]
... [truncated]
```

/// Classifies a MIR call terminator into one of the lockdep-relevant effects.
fn classify_call_effect<'tcx>(
    tcx: TyCtxt<'tcx>,
    current_def_id: DefId,
    body: &Body<'tcx>,
    state: &BlockState<'tcx>,
    call: Option<&rustc_middle::mir::TerminatorKind<'tcx>>,
) -> Option<CallEffect<'tcx>> {
    let rustc_middle::mir::TerminatorKind::Call {
        func,
        args,
        destination,
        ..
    } = call?
    else {
        return None;
    };

    let (def_id, _) = func.const_fn_def()?;
    let item_name = tcx.item_name(def_id);
    let method_name = item_name.as_str();
    let callee_path = tcx.def_path_str(def_id);

... [truncated]

```text
        for analysis in analyses {
            let mut merged = summaries
                .get(&analysis.def_id)
                .cloned()
                .unwrap_or_default();
            for callsite in analysis.callsites.iter().filter(|callsite| callsite.held_locks.is_empty())
            {
                if let Some(callee_locks) = summaries.get(&callsite.callee) {
                    let previous_len = merged.len();
                    merged.extend(
                        callee_locks
                            .iter()
                            .filter_map(|lock| rebind_lock_info(lock, &callsite.arg_bindings)),
                    );
                    changed |= merged.len() != previous_len;
                }
            }
            summaries.insert(analysis.def_id, merged);
        }
    }

    summaries
}

   162	    /// A connecting socket can become obsolete because some network events can set the socket to
   163	    /// connected state (if the connection succeeds) or initial state (if the connection is

   178	            let State::Connecting(connecting_stream) = owned_state else {
   179	                unreachable!("`State::Connecting` is checked before calling `borrow_result`");
   180	            };
   181	
   182	            match connecting_stream.into_result() {

// SPDX-License-Identifier: MPL-2.0

//! MIR-based fact collection for the lockdep prototype.
//!
//! This module is responsible for:

fn collect_call_arg_bindings<'tcx>(
    tcx: TyCtxt<'tcx>,
    current_def_id: DefId,
    body: &Body<'tcx>,
    state: &BlockState<'tcx>,
    args: &[Spanned<Operand<'tcx>>],
) -> BTreeMap<usize, LockClassKey> {
    args.iter()
        .enumerate()
        .filter_map(|(index, argument)| {
            bind_call_argument(tcx, current_def_id, body, state, &argument.node)
                .map(|class| (index + 1, class))
        })
        .collect()
}

    state: &BlockState<'tcx>,
... [truncated]
```

#### Assistant · commentary · 2026-03-25 02:31:25 UTC

I have located the main gap: it is not that the code does not have these sequences, but that many sequences obtain the first lock through the "helper/wrapper that returns guard". Currently, lockdep will only call it as a normal function, and the subsequent second lock cannot be connected. I plan to first connect the `wrappers` configuration to the analysis, and then fill in the `lockdep.toml` with the wrappers used by `aster-kernel`.

... [truncated]

/// Computes per-basic-block incoming state for the current MIR body.
fn compute_block_states<'tcx>(
    tcx: TyCtxt<'tcx>,
    current_def_id: DefId,
    body: &Body<'tcx>,
    base_context: ContextKind,
) -> Vec<Option<BlockState<'tcx>>> {
    let mut in_states = vec![None; body.basic_blocks.len()];
    let mut entry_state = BlockState::empty();

+                if uid == posix_thread.credentials().ruid() {
+                    processes.push(process);
+                }
+            }
             if processes.is_empty() {
                 return_errno!(Errno::ESRCH);
             }
             processes
         }
*** End Patch
```

</details>

@@
         }
         PriorityTarget::User(uid) => {
             // Get the processes that are running under the specified user
             // Lock order: PID table -> tasks of process.

#### Assistant · final_answer · 2026-03-25 02:42:07 UTC

Non-`lockdep` changes have been rolled back. Currently, only these 3 lockdep related modifications are retained:
[lockdep.toml](/root/asterinas-codex/lockdep.toml)
[main.rs](/root/asterinas-codex/tools/lockdep/src/main.rs)
[collect.rs](/root/asterinas-codex/tools/lockdep/analysis/src/collect.rs)What I did was to change `wrappers` from "only parsing but not taking effect" to "recording the returned guard as a held lock at the call point", and added configuration to the common guard-wrapper in `aster-kernel`. After re-running, the lockdep result of `aster-kernel` is 2439 lock events and 637 lock edges; many sequences that were originally lost due to wrappers such as `pid_table_mut`, `ProcessGroup::lock`, `Session::lock`, and `write_updated_state` can now be entered into the graph.For the rest that cannot be found clearly, I will directly explain them as limitations according to your request:1. [get_priority.rs:55](/root/asterinas-codex/kernel/src/syscall/get_priority.rs#L55) This `PID table -> tasks of process` still does not appear stably in the graph.Reason: Currently lockdep cannot propagate the "lock obtained through wrapper" through iterator adapter and closure capture; this is exactly the form of `pid_table_mut().iter_processes().filter(...)`.2. The document-level `Parent Before Child` rule in [systree_node.rs:37](/root/asterinas-codex/kernel/src/fs/fs_impls/cgroupfs/systree_node.rs#L37) is currently not guaranteed to be explicitly dropped in the graph.Reason: The relevant sequence is mainly hidden in the inheritance/macro expansion helper path of `aster_systree`. Currently lockdep only does direct local call summary and will not restore such inherited helper path to the explicit parent-lock -> child-lock edge.

The conclusion is: Under the premise of "not changing the kernel code", I have filled the wrapper gaps that can be filled by changing `lockdep` itself; the remaining gaps that are not covered are indeed the limits of the current analyzer's capabilities, and should not be made up by changing `aster-kernel`.

fn collect_entry_contexts<'tcx>(tcx: TyCtxt<'tcx>) -> HashMap<DefId, Vec<ContextKind>> {
    let mut map: HashMap<DefId, BTreeSet<ContextKind>> = HashMap::new();
    let configured_entries = load_configured_irq_entries();

    for local_def_id in tcx.mir_keys(()) {
        let def_id = local_def_id.to_def_id();
        if !tcx.def_kind(def_id).is_fn_like() {
            continue;
        }
        if tcx.visibility(def_id).is_public() {
            map.entry(def_id).or_default().insert(ContextKind::Task);
        }
        let body = tcx.optimized_mir(def_id);
        let callable_locals = collect_callable_locals(body);

        for block_data in body.basic_blocks.iter() {
            let Some(terminator) = &block_data.terminator else {
                continue;
            };
            let TerminatorKind::Call { func, args, .. } = &terminator.kind else {
                continue;
... [truncated]
```

#### Assistant · final_answer · 2026-03-25 02:47:32 UTC

[`lockdep.toml`](/root/asterinas-codex/lockdep.toml) is the workspace-level configuration file of `tools/lockdep`. Currently, only two types of configurations are used in this document: `irq_entries` and `wrappers`.`[[irq_entries]]` means "treat a function call as a context entry, and mark a callback function it receives into the specified context." The field is defined in [tools/lockdep/src/main.rs:222](/root/asterinas-codex/tools/lockdep/src/main.rs#L222), and the actual usage is in [tools/lockdep/analysis/src/collect.rs:1619](/root/asterinas-codex/tools/lockdep/analysis/src/collect.rs#L1619).
The current one:[`lockdep.toml:1`](/root/asterinas-codex/lockdep.toml#L1)
means:
- `function = "SoftIrqLine::enable"`: matches the `def_path` of this called function.
- `context = "BottomHalfL1"`: The callback registered in it is regarded as running in the context of `BottomHalfL1`.
- `callback_arg_index = 1`: This is the parameter index in the current implementation, starting from 0, so `1` means "the second parameter is the callback".The meaning of `[[wrappers]]` is "tell lockdep: this function itself is not directly `.lock()/.read()/.write()`, but what it returns is actually an already taken guard. Calling it is equivalent to acquiring a lock."The configuration will be read from TOML first and then passed to the analyzer through environment variables, see [tools/lockdep/src/main.rs:299](/root/asterinas-codex/tools/lockdep/src/main.rs#L299);The locations that really take effect are [tools/lockdep/analysis/src/collect.rs:129](/root/asterinas-codex/tools/lockdep/analysis/src/collect.rs#L129) and [tools/lockdep/analysis/src/collect.rs:610](/root/asterinas-codex/tools/lockdep/analysis/src/collect.rs#L610).
Field meaning is:
- `function`: wrapper's own complete function path.- `acquire`: It is equivalent to the underlying acquire. Typical values ​​are `lock`, `read` and `write`.
- `release`: In the current implementation, it is only a reserved field, which semantically represents the release method of guard; but now the analysis actually relies on guard `drop` in MIR to identify release, and this field has not really participated in release modeling.The wrappers in your current file are:
- [`lockdep.toml:6`](/root/asterinas-codex/lockdep.toml#L6) `process::pid_table::pid_table_mut`
  Indicates that calling it is equivalent to getting `PID_TABLE.lock()`.
- [`lockdep.toml:11`](/root/asterinas-codex/lockdep.toml#L11) `ParentProcess::lock`
  Indicates getting the mutex guard inside the parent structure.- [`lockdep.toml:16`](/root/asterinas-codex/lockdep.toml#L16) `ProcessGroup::lock`
  Indicates getting the mutex guard of process group inner.
- [`lockdep.toml:21`](/root/asterinas-codex/lockdep.toml#L21) `Session::lock`
  Indicates getting the mutex guard of session inner.- [`lockdep.toml:26`](/root/asterinas-codex/lockdep.toml#L26) `StreamSocket::write_updated_state`
  It means that although it is a helper, it returns the guard of `state.write()`, so it is processed as `write`.
- [`lockdep.toml:31`](/root/asterinas-codex/lockdep.toml#L31) `CgroupMembership::read_lock`
  Indicates that the read lock of global membership is obtained.- [`lockdep.toml:36`](/root/asterinas-codex/lockdep.toml#L36) `CgroupMembership::write_lock`
  Indicates that the write lock of global membership is obtained.

In one sentence:
- `irq_entries` are "entry context annotations".
- `wrappers` is a "helper that returns guard as a real acquire".

If you are willing, I can next map each configuration in this `lockdep.toml` to the specific code call point and explain why it needs to exist one by one.

## Configuration

The current `lockdep.toml` support is intentionally minimal.

Supported today:

- automatic loading from workspace root
- explicit `--config <path>`
- config summary counts in output
- `ignore` prefixes affecting which functions are retained in the summarized result set
- `irq_entries` affecting IRQ entry-context detection

Parsed but not yet applied to analysis:

- `wrappers`
- `ordered_helpers`

/// Loads the optional `lockdep.toml` file and prepares a user-facing config report.
fn load_lockdep_config(
    workspace_root: &Path,
    config_path: Option<&Path>,
) -> Result<(LockdepConfig, ConfigReport), Box<dyn std::error::Error>> {
    let path = config_path
        .map(|path| {
            if path.is_absolute() {
                path.to_path_buf()
            } else {
                workspace_root.join(path)
            }
        })
        .unwrap_or_else(|| workspace_root.join("lockdep.toml"));
    if !path.exists() {
        return Ok((
            LockdepConfig::default(),
            ConfigReport {
                path: None,
                ignore_count: 0,
... [truncated]

/// Applies `ignore` prefix filters from configuration to function summaries.
fn apply_ignore_filters(crates: &mut [AnalysisArtifact], ignore_prefixes: &[String]) {
    if ignore_prefixes.is_empty() {
        return;
    }

    for crate_artifact in crates {
        crate_artifact.functions.retain(|function| {
            !ignore_prefixes
                .iter()
                .any(|prefix| function.def_path.starts_with(prefix))
```

*** Begin Patch
*** Add File: /root/asterinas-codex/tools/lockdep/lockdep-toml.md
+# `lockdep.toml` Format
+
+This document explains the workspace-level `lockdep.toml` file used by
+`tools/lockdep`.
+
+## Where It Is Loaded
+
+By default, `cargo-lockdep` looks for `lockdep.toml` at the workspace root.
+
+Examples:
+
+```bash
+cargo run --manifest-path tools/lockdep/Cargo.toml -- \
+  -p aster-kernel --target x86_64-unknown-none -- --quiet
+```
+
+This automatically loads:
+
+```text
+<workspace-root>/lockdep.toml
+```
+
+You may also pass an explicit path:
+
+```bash
+cargo run --manifest-path tools/lockdep/Cargo.toml -- \
+  --config lockdep.toml \
+  -p aster-kernel --target x86_64-unknown-none -- --quiet
+```
+
+If the file does not exist, lockdep runs with an empty configuration.
+
+## Top-Level Structure
+
+The current parser accepts these top-level keys:
+
+```toml
+ignore = [
... [truncated]
```

## Configuration

```bash

<summary>Tool · 2026-03-25 02:55:23 UTC · `exec_command` `/usr/bin/zsh -lc "sed -n '340,460p' tools/lockdep/progress.md"`</summary>

- Time: `2026-03-25 02:55:23 UTC`
- Exit code: `0`

```text

- Lock-class identity is improved, but still not fully instance-sensitive.
- `RwLock` / `RwMutex` mode compatibility is only partially modeled.
- Ordered double-lock helpers are only heuristically normalized.
- IRQ conflict checking is not yet implemented in lockdep style.
- Annotation/config-based precision mechanisms are only planned, not implemented.

## Recommended Next Work

The most valuable next steps are:

1. Stabilize lock-class identity.
2. Add lock-mode compatibility filtering for `read`/`write`.
3. Implement ordered multi-lock annotation/config support.
4. Add real IRQ safety conflict checks.

These four steps are the shortest path from “useful prototype” to “actionable kernel deadlock detector”.

## Current Triage Snapshot

Recent `aster-kernel` results after the latest precision fixes:

- lock events: `2209`
- function-level lock edges: `878`
... [truncated]
```

# Lockdep Summary

This file summarizes the current state of the static lockdep prototype in this repository.

## Current State

The current implementation lives under [tools/lockdep](/root/asterinas-codex/tools/lockdep).

The prototype can already:

- build as an independent tool via `cargo run --manifest-path tools/lockdep/Cargo.toml -- ...`
- analyze real `ostd` and `aster-kernel` crates on `x86_64-unknown-none`
- export per-crate artifacts and aggregate them into a global report
- emit:
  - human-readable terminal output
  - JSON output
  - DOT graph output

- plan: [plan.md](/root/asterinas-codex/tools/lockdep/plan.md)
- progress tracker: [progress.md](/root/asterinas-codex/tools/lockdep/progress.md)

- Time: `2026-03-25 02:56:11 UTC`

```text
# cargo-lockdep

`cargo-lockdep` is a prototype static lock dependency analyzer for Asterinas.

It is currently implemented as an independent tool crate under
[tools/lockdep](/root/asterinas-codex/tools/lockdep).

The tool can be invoked directly, and it is also wired into OSDK as
`cargo osdk lockdep`.

Direct entrypoint:

```bash
cargo run --manifest-path tools/lockdep/Cargo.toml -- --help
```

OSDK entrypoint:

```bash
cargo osdk lockdep --help
```

## What It Does

... [truncated]
```

</details>

```text
# Lockdep Cycle Review

This document reviews the 5 cycles currently reported by the static lockdep prototype
against `aster-kernel` on `x86_64-unknown-none`.

## Summary

Current conclusion:

- Cycle 1 (`futex::lock_bucket_pairs`): false positive.
- Cycle 2 (`exfat::rename` / `ExfatFs::evict_inode`): false positive.
- Cycle 3 (`VsockSpace::poll`): false positive.
- Cycle 4 (`ext2::read_lock_two_inodes`): false positive.
- Cycle 5 (`ext2::write_lock_two_inodes`): false positive.

The reported 5 cycles are useful because they expose real precision problems in the analyzer,
but they do not currently look like actionable deadlocks in the kernel.

The false positives fall into three buckets:

1. Missing path sensitivity for ordered double-lock helpers.
2. Missing lock-mode compatibility for `RwLock` / `RwMutex`.
3. Unstable lock-class identity for local MIR places such as `(*_4)`.

... [truncated]
```

</details>

# Lockdep 报告复核

日期：2026-03-24

本文件复核了当前分支对所有直接依赖 `ostd` 的 crate 运行 `lockdep` 后得到的告警。

本次全量结果：

- 3 个 `cycle`
- 1 个 `irq conflict`
- 4 个 `aa/self-loop`

注意：这 8 条并不是 8 个彼此独立的问题。其中：

- `cycle 1` 和 `aa deadlock 1` 指向同一个 epoll 位置；
- `cycle 3` 和 `aa deadlock 3` 指向同一个 overlayfs 位置；
- `irq conflict 1` 和 `aa deadlock 4` 指向同一个 IRQ 重入类问题。

## 总结

结论如下：

- 真实问题：1 条
- 误报：7 条
... [truncated]

# `lockdep.toml` Format

This document explains the workspace-level `lockdep.toml` file used by
`tools/lockdep`.

## Where It Is Loaded

By default, `cargo-lockdep` looks for `lockdep.toml` at the workspace root.

Examples:

```bash
cargo run --manifest-path tools/lockdep/Cargo.toml -- \
  -p aster-kernel --target x86_64-unknown-none -- --quiet
```

This automatically loads:

```text
<workspace-root>/lockdep.toml
```

You may also pass an explicit path:

... [truncated]

```text
/// Collects the full crate artifact from MIR bodies in the current crate.
pub fn collect_artifact<'tcx>(tcx: TyCtxt<'tcx>) -> AnalysisArtifact {
    let crate_name = tcx.crate_name(LOCAL_CRATE).to_string();
    let package_name = env::var("CARGO_PKG_NAME").unwrap_or_else(|_| crate_name.clone());
    let manifest_dir = env::var("CARGO_MANIFEST_DIR").unwrap_or_default();
    let target = env::var("TARGET").ok();
    let is_primary_package = env::var("CARGO_PRIMARY_PACKAGE").is_ok();
    let configured_wrappers = load_configured_wrappers();
    let wrapper_def_ids = resolve_wrapper_def_ids(tcx, &configured_wrappers);
    let wrapper_entry_locks = compute_wrapper_entry_locks(tcx, &wrapper_def_ids);

    let entry_contexts = collect_entry_contexts(tcx);
    let direct_calls = collect_direct_calls(tcx);
    let propagated_contexts = propagate_contexts(&entry_contexts, &direct_calls);

    let analyses = tcx
        .mir_keys(())
        .iter()
        .filter(|local_def_id| tcx.def_kind(local_def_id.to_def_id()).is_fn_like())
        .map(|local_def_id| {
            let def_id = local_def_id.to_def_id();
            let body = tcx.optimized_mir(def_id);
            let location = span_to_location(tcx, tcx.def_span(def_id));
            let contexts = propagated_contexts
... [truncated]
```

    wrapper_entry_locks: &HashMap<DefId, LockInfoArtifact>,
) -> Option<CallSite> {

        return None;
    };
    let (callee, _) = func.const_fn_def()?;
    if wrapper_entry_locks.contains_key(&callee) {
        return None;

        return None;

#### Assistant · final_answer · 2026-03-25 03:08:09 UTC

It can be analyzed clearly and the conclusion is divided into two levels.

You cannot directly remove `wrappers` now. The evidence is very direct: I used the same `aster-kernel`, only removed `wrappers` from the configuration and ran `tools/lockdep` again.

Comparison of results:
- There are `wrappers`: 2439 lock events, 637 edges
- No `wrappers`: 2245 lock events, 553 edges

In other words, removing it will reduce 194 events and 84 edges.What is lost is not the marginal information, but the lock order clearly written in many comments. Typical example:
- `PID table -> tasks of process` of [execve.rs:237](/root/asterinas-codex/kernel/src/process/execve.rs#L237)
  - Without `wrappers`, `make_current_main_thread` has only 2 events and 0 edges
  - When there are `wrappers`, it becomes 4 events and 3 edges- `PID table -> process group` of [init_proc.rs:115](/root/asterinas-codex/kernel/src/process/process/init_proc.rs#L115)
  - Without `wrappers`, `set_session_and_group` only has the second half of the local edge
  - When there are `wrappers`, the guard returned by `pid_table_mut()` can also be included- `write_updated_state()` of [stream/mod.rs:169](/root/asterinas-codex/kernel/src/net/socket/ip/stream/mod.rs#L169)
  - Without `wrappers`, `set_option` cannot see `state -> options`
  - With `wrappers`, this edge can be restoredThe root cause is that currently lockdep does not yet have a general modeling of "the function returns with an acquired lock". Your current implementation also specifies this gap:
- `return-with-lock modeling` is still listed as missing in [summary.md](/root/asterinas-codex/tools/lockdep/summary.md)
- [progress.md](/root/asterinas-codex/tools/lockdep/progress.md) also clearly states that the summary model does not yet support `returns_with_locks`- And these wrappers in the warehouse have exactly this pattern:
  - [pid_table.rs:348](/root/asterinas-codex/kernel/src/process/pid_table.rs#L348) `pid_table_mut() -> MutexGuard`
  - [session.rs:61](/root/asterinas-codex/kernel/src/process/process/session.rs#L61) `Session::lock() -> SessionGuard`- [process_group.rs:56](/root/asterinas-codex/kernel/src/process/process/process_group.rs#L56) `ProcessGroup::lock() -> ProcessGroupGuard`
  - [stream/mod.rs:169](/root/asterinas-codex/kernel/src/net/socket/ip/stream/mod.rs#L169) `write_updated_state() -> RwLockWriteGuard`So, `wrappers` is now essentially a "parser gap" configuration, not something that is theoretically required by lockdep.

Can it be finally removed? Yes, but the premise is to replenish the capabilities first, not directly delete the configuration. Do at least one of the following:
1. Implement general `returns_with_locks`/return-with-lock digest propagation.
2. Automatically identify trivial wrapper: take the lock in the function body and return the guard directly.
3. Do stronger cross-function inline analysis for such small functions.

If these are done, most of the `wrappers` currently in `lockdep.toml` can disappear, or at least be downgraded to "cover configurations".But I don’t recommend deleting it now. It has clear value at this stage, and configuration declarations also have a practical benefit: when the analyzer cannot push certain wrappers, developers can explicitly supplement them without having to change the analyzer code every time.

One sentence conclusion:
- Now: It cannot be removed. If you remove it, it will obviously lose its edge.
- Long term: It can be made optional, but only if automatic modeling of return-with-lock is implemented first.
- In addition, the `release` field in `wrappers` currently does not really participate in release modeling. This field can be simplified if viewed alone; but the `wrappers` mechanism itself cannot be deleted yet.If you want, I can give you a list of "minimum alternative wrappers implementation solutions" in the next step, ranking them in ascending order of project volume.

## Turn 13

- Turn ID: `019d22f7-7877-7d71-b953-f49b5e8082df`
- Start: `2026-03-25 03:08:56 UTC`
- End: `2026-03-25 03:09:16 UTC`

### Timeline

#### User · 2026-03-25 03:08:56 UTC

> Will the lock's life cycle now be limited to the function? No way to get back out?

#### Assistant · final_answer · 2026-03-25 03:09:16 UTC

Yes, in the current implementation, the lock life cycle is basically limited to the function body by default; what the analyzer can natively and stably track is the situation of "acquire in this function, continue to hold it later, and then form an edge or drop in this function".

From an implementation point of view, the current direct modeling is within the function:
- acquire/release event
- held-lock collection
- edge generated based on held-lock collectionThe corresponding location is [collect.rs](/root/asterinas-codex/tools/lockdep/analysis/src/collect.rs):
- `classify_call_effect` only identifies the current call as acquire/release/alias
- `apply_effect` puts the lock into the current `BlockState.guards`
- `emit_effect` generates edge using current `state.guards`The real cross-function propagation is now "call point summary propagation", but what is propagated is `entry_locks`, not "which locks are still held when returning". The relevant logic is:
[collect.rs](/root/asterinas-codex/tools/lockdep/analysis/src/collect.rs#L760)
and
[collect.rs](/root/asterinas-codex/tools/lockdep/analysis/src/collect.rs#L782)That is to say, currently supported are:
- "I already hold A in caller, and then call callee, and callee will take B as soon as it enters"
- thus complementing `A -> B`

But universal ones are not currently supported:
- "callee returns a guard, and caller uses this return value to continue to obtain a lock"This is where `returns_with_locks` / return-with-lock modeling falls short. The documentation also clearly states that this is still missing:
[summary.md](/root/asterinas-codex/tools/lockdep/summary.md#L183)
[progress.md](/root/asterinas-codex/tools/lockdep/progress.md#L217)
[plan.md](/root/asterinas-codex/tools/lockdep/plan.md#L357)So the answer is:
- By default: it cannot be returned, and life cycle analysis basically stops within the function.
- Exception: A small number of "guard-returning helpers" are now explicitly patch-modeled via `wrappers` in `lockdep.toml`, so these specific functions can "appear to return the lock".比如：
- [pid_table_mut](/root/asterinas-codex/kernel/src/process/pid_table.rs#L348)
- [Session::lock](/root/asterinas-codex/kernel/src/process/process/session.rs#L61)
- [ProcessGroup::lock](/root/asterinas-codex/kernel/src/process/process/process_group.rs#L56)- [write_updated_state](/root/asterinas-codex/kernel/src/net/socket/ip/stream/mod.rs#L169)

These are not "return locks" supported by the parser in general, but are connected specifically by `wrappers`.

fn compute_wrapper_entry_locks<'tcx>(
    tcx: TyCtxt<'tcx>,
    wrapper_def_ids: &HashMap<DefId, ConfiguredWrapper>,
) -> HashMap<DefId, LockInfoArtifact> {
    if wrapper_def_ids.is_empty() {
        return HashMap::new();
    }

    let empty_wrappers = HashMap::new();

    wrapper_def_ids
        .iter()
        .filter_map(|(def_id, wrapper)| {
            let body = tcx.optimized_mir(*def_id);
            let analysis = analyze_body(tcx, *def_id, body, ContextKind::Task, &empty_wrappers);
... [truncated]
```

<summary>Tool · 2026-03-25 03:10:04 UTC · `exec_command` `/usr/bin/zsh -lc "sed -n '720,860p' tools/lockdep/analysis/src/collect.rs"`</summary>

```text
    args: GenericArgsRef<'tcx>,
    method_name: &str,
) -> String {
    let item_name = tcx.item_name(adt.did());
    let primitive = item_name.as_str();
    if primitive == "Mutex" || primitive == "RwMutex" {
        return "Sleeping".into();
    }

    let guardian = args
        .types()
        .nth(1)
        .map(|ty| short_type_name(tcx, peel_refs(ty)))
        .unwrap_or_else(|| "Unknown".into());

    if primitive == "RwLock" && guardian == "WriteIrqDisabled" && method_name == "read" {
        "PreemptDisabled".into()
    } else {
        guardian
    }
}

    tcx: TyCtxt<'tcx>,

        let mut state = in_states[block.as_usize()]
            .clone()

/// Computes per-basic-block incoming state for the current MIR body.
fn compute_block_states<'tcx>(
    tcx: TyCtxt<'tcx>,
    current_def_id: DefId,
    body: &Body<'tcx>,
    base_context: ContextKind,
    wrapper_entry_locks: &HashMap<DefId, LockInfoArtifact>,
) -> Vec<Option<BlockState<'tcx>>> {
    let mut in_states = vec![None; body.basic_blocks.len()];
    let mut entry_state = BlockState::empty();
    if base_context == ContextKind::BottomHalfL1
        && body.arg_count >= 1
        && short_type_name(tcx, peel_refs(body.local_decls[Local::from_usize(1)].ty))
            == "DisabledLocalIrqGuard"
    {
... [truncated]

/// Classifies a MIR call terminator into one of the lockdep-relevant effects.
fn classify_call_effect<'tcx>(
    tcx: TyCtxt<'tcx>,
    current_def_id: DefId,
    body: &Body<'tcx>,
    state: &BlockState<'tcx>,
    call: Option<&rustc_middle::mir::TerminatorKind<'tcx>>,
    wrapper_entry_locks: &HashMap<DefId, LockInfoArtifact>,
) -> Option<CallEffect<'tcx>> {
    let rustc_middle::mir::TerminatorKind::Call {
        func,
        args,
        destination,
        ..
    } = call?
    else {
        return None;
    };

    let (def_id, _) = func.const_fn_def()?;
... [truncated]
```

/// A spin lock.
///
/// # Guard behavior
///
/// The type `G' specifies the guard behavior of the spin lock. While holding the lock,
/// - if `G` is [`PreemptDisabled`], preemption is disabled;
/// - if `G` is [`LocalIrqDisabled`], local IRQs are disabled.
///
/// The `G` can also be provided by other crates other than ostd,
/// if it behaves similar like [`PreemptDisabled`] or [`LocalIrqDisabled`].
///
... [truncated]

#### Assistant · final_answer · 2026-03-25 03:29:23 UTC

Implemented, and `wrappers` have now been removed.

The core changes are in [collect.rs](/root/asterinas-codex/tools/lockdep/analysis/src/collect.rs). Now the analyzer will:
- Summary of iterative calculation function "locks still held on return"
- Rebind this type of return lock to the actual parameter/`self` at the call site
- Continue to include the returned guard into the caller's held-lock collectionThis solves the problem that guard-returning helpers such as `pid_table_mut()`, `Session::lock()`, `ProcessGroup::lock()` and `write_updated_state()` had to be hard-coded through `wrappers` configuration.I also deleted the `wrappers` configuration channel:
- All `wrappers` have been removed from [lockdep.toml](/root/asterinas-codex/lockdep.toml)
- `wrappers` parsing, environment variable passing and count output have been removed from [main.rs](/root/asterinas-codex/tools/lockdep/src/main.rs)- [lockdep-toml.md](/root/asterinas-codex/tools/lockdep/lockdep-toml.md) and other documents have been updated to "return-with-lock has taken effect and `wrappers` are no longer needed"I also added a regression test to specifically cover the path of "callee returns `SpinLockGuard`, and caller takes the second lock":
[fixture_cases.rs](/root/asterinas-codex/tools/lockdep/tests/fixture_cases.rs)
[lib.rs](/root/asterinas-codex/tools/lockdep/tests/fixtures/ostd-lockdep-cases/src/lib.rs)Verification results:
- `cargo test --manifest-path tools/lockdep/Cargo.toml --test fixture_cases` passed
- For `aster-kernel`, the configuration results are exactly the same with or without `wrappers`:
  - Both have 2489 lock events, 807 lock edges, 1 cycle, and 1 AA/self-loop
- The 24 crates that fully depend on `ostd` can also run normally.Now this feature is not a "completely general system of return lock semantics", but `wrappers` are no longer needed for the current class of guard-returning helpers. If you want, I can submit these changes into a commit in the next step.

```text
// SPDX-License-Identifier: MPL-2.0

use std::{
    fs,
    path::{Path, PathBuf},
    process::Command,
    time::{SystemTime, UNIX_EPOCH},
};

use serde_json::Value;

fn fixture_manifest() -> PathBuf {
    Path::new(env!("CARGO_MANIFEST_DIR"))
        .join("tests")
        .join("fixtures")
        .join("ostd-lockdep-cases")
        .join("Cargo.toml")
}

fn temp_json_path() -> PathBuf {
    let nanos = SystemTime::now()

// SPDX-License-Identifier: MPL-2.0

//! MIR-based fact collection for the lockdep prototype.

+// SPDX-License-Identifier: MPL-2.0
+
+use super::*;
+
+/// Execution contexts currently recognized by the prototype.
+#[derive(Clone, Copy, Debug, PartialEq, Eq, PartialOrd, Ord)]
+pub(super) enum ContextKind {
+    Task,
+    TaskIrqDisabled,
+    HardIrqTopHalf,
+    BottomHalfL1,
+    BottomHalfL1IrqDisabled,
+    BottomHalfL2,
+}
+
+pub(super) fn softirq_entry_state_for_body<'tcx>(
+    tcx: TyCtxt<'tcx>,
+    body: &Body<'tcx>,
+    base_context: ContextKind,
+) -> BlockState<'tcx> {
+    let mut entry_state = BlockState::empty();
+    if base_context == ContextKind::BottomHalfL1
+        && body.arg_count >= 1
+        && short_type_name(tcx, place::peel_refs(body.local_decls[Local::from_usize(1)].ty))
+            == "DisabledLocalIrqGuard"
+    {
+        entry_state.irq_guard_locals.insert(Local::from_usize(1));
+    }
+    entry_state
+}
+
+pub(super) fn current_context(state: &BlockState<'_>, base_context: ContextKind) -> ContextKind {
+    if state.irq_guard_locals.is_empty() {
+        base_context
+    } else if matches!(base_context, ContextKind::Task) {
+        ContextKind::TaskIrqDisabled
+    } else if matches!(base_context, ContextKind::BottomHalfL1) {
+        ContextKind::BottomHalfL1IrqDisabled
... [truncated]

+// SPDX-License-Identifier: MPL-2.0

+use super::*;

+pub(super) fn dedup_edges(edges: &mut Vec<LockEdgeArtifact>) {
+    edges.sort_by(|left, right| {
+        left.context
+            .cmp(&right.context)
+            .then(left.from.class.cmp(&right.from.class))
+            .then(left.from.primitive.cmp(&right.from.primitive))
+            .then(left.from.acquire.cmp(&right.from.acquire))
+            .then(left.to.class.cmp(&right.to.class))
+            .then(left.to.primitive.cmp(&right.to.primitive))
+            .then(left.to.acquire.cmp(&right.to.acquire))
+            .then(left.location.cmp(&right.location))
+    });
+    edges.dedup_by(|left, right| {
+        left.context == right.context
+            && left.from == right.from
+            && left.to == right.to
+            && left.location == right.location
+    });
+}
+
+pub(super) fn release_local<'tcx>(state: &mut BlockState<'tcx>, local: Local, _reason: &str) {
+    state.aliases.remove(&local);
+    state.guards.remove(&local);
+    state.irq_guard_locals.remove(&local);
+    state.local_origins.remove(&local);
+}
+
+pub(super) fn resolve_alias<'tcx>(state: &BlockState<'tcx>, place: Place<'tcx>) -> Place<'tcx> {
+    let Some(local) = place.as_local() else {
+        return place;
+    };
+    state.aliases.get(&local).copied().unwrap_or(place)
+}
+
... [truncated]

*** Add File: /root/asterinas-codex/tools/lockdep/analysis/src/collect/summary.rs
+// SPDX-License-Identifier: MPL-2.0
+
+use super::*;
+
+pub(super) fn collect_direct_calls<'tcx>(tcx: TyCtxt<'tcx>) -> HashMap<DefId, HashSet<DefId>> {
+    let mut graph = HashMap::<DefId, HashSet<DefId>>::new();
+
+    for local_def_id in tcx.mir_keys(()) {
+        let caller = local_def_id.to_def_id();
+        if !tcx.def_kind(caller).is_fn_like() {
+            continue;
+        }
+
+        let body = tcx.optimized_mir(caller);
+        let mut callees = HashSet::new();
+        for block_data in body.basic_blocks.iter() {
+            let Some(terminator) = &block_data.terminator else {
+                continue;
+            };
+            let TerminatorKind::Call { func, .. } = &terminator.kind else {
+                continue;
+            };
+            let Some((callee, _)) = func.const_fn_def() else {
+                continue;
+            };
+            if callee.is_local() && tcx.def_kind(callee).is_fn_like() {
+                callees.insert(callee);
+            }
+        }
+        graph.insert(caller, callees);
+    }
+
+    graph
+}
+
+pub(super) fn propagate_contexts(
+    entry_contexts: &HashMap<DefId, Vec<context::ContextKind>>,
+    direct_calls: &HashMap<DefId, HashSet<DefId>>,
... [truncated]
```

// SPDX-License-Identifier: MPL-2.0

use super::*;

pub(super) fn dedup_edges(edges: &mut Vec<LockEdgeArtifact>) {
    edges.sort_by(|left, right| {
        left.context
            .cmp(&right.context)
            .then(left.from.class.cmp(&right.from.class))
            .then(left.from.primitive.cmp(&right.from.primitive))
            .then(left.from.acquire.cmp(&right.from.acquire))
            .then(left.to.class.cmp(&right.to.class))
            .then(left.to.primitive.cmp(&right.to.primitive))
            .then(left.to.acquire.cmp(&right.to.acquire))
            .then(left.location.cmp(&right.location))
    });
    edges.dedup_by(|left, right| {
        left.context == right.context
            && left.from == right.from
            && left.to == right.to
            && left.location == right.location
    });

```text
// SPDX-License-Identifier: MPL-2.0

use super::*;

pub(super) fn compute_block_states<'tcx>(
    tcx: TyCtxt<'tcx>,
    current_def_id: DefId,
    body: &Body<'tcx>,
    base_context: context::ContextKind,
    return_lock_summaries: &HashMap<DefId, BTreeSet<LockInfoArtifact>>,
) -> Vec<Option<BlockState<'tcx>>> {
    let mut in_states = vec![None; body.basic_blocks.len()];
    in_states[BasicBlock::from_usize(0).as_usize()] =
        Some(context::softirq_entry_state_for_body(tcx, body, base_context));

    let predecessors = body.basic_blocks.predecessors().clone();
    let mut queue = VecDeque::from([BasicBlock::from_usize(0)]);

    while let Some(block) = queue.pop_front() {
        let mut state = in_states[block.as_usize()]
            .clone()
            .unwrap_or_else(BlockState::empty);

        let block_data = &body[block];
... [truncated]
```

```text
    }
}

fn classify_lock_call<'tcx>(
    tcx: TyCtxt<'tcx>,
    current_def_id: DefId,
    body: &Body<'tcx>,
    state: &BlockState<'tcx>,
    receiver: Place<'tcx>,
    receiver_ty: Ty<'tcx>,
    method_name: &str,
) -> Option<LockInfoArtifact> {
    let lock_ty = place::peel_refs(receiver_ty);
    let ty::Adt(adt, args) = lock_ty.kind() else {
        return None;
    };
    let primitive = tcx.item_name(adt.did()).to_string();

    let acquire = match (&*primitive, method_name) {
        ("SpinLock", "lock" | "try_lock")
        | ("RwLock", "read" | "write" | "try_read" | "try_write")
        | ("Mutex", "lock" | "try_lock")
        | ("RwMutex", "read" | "write" | "try_read" | "try_write") => method_name.to_string(),
        _ => return None,
... [truncated]
```

impl FileName {
    pub fn is_real(&self) -> bool {
        use FileName::*;
        match *self {
            Real(_) => true,
            Anon(_)
            | MacroExpansion(_)
            | ProcMacroSourceCode(_)
            | CliCrateAttr(_)
            | Custom(_)
            | CfgSpec(_)
            | DocTest(_, _)
            | InlineAsm(_) => false,
        }
    }

fn deref_ty<'tcx>(ty: Ty<'tcx>) -> Option<Ty<'tcx>> {
    ty.builtin_deref(true)

fn field_identity<'tcx>(
    owner_ty: Ty<'tcx>,
    downcast_variant: Option<usize>,
    field_index: rustc_abi::FieldIdx,
) -> (String, String) {
    match owner_ty.kind() {
        ty::Adt(adt, _) => {
            let owner_ty_name = type_key(owner_ty);
            let field_name = if adt.is_enum() {
                downcast_variant
                    .and_then(|variant_index| adt.variants().iter().nth(variant_index))
                    .and_then(|variant| variant.fields.get(field_index))
                    .map(|field| field.name.to_string())
            } else {
                adt.all_fields()
                    .nth(field_index.index())
                    .map(|field| field.name.to_string())
            }
... [truncated]

#### Assistant · commentary · 2026-03-25 04:00:27 UTC

#### Assistant · commentary · 2026-03-25 04:02:58 UTC

I located a more likely root cause: the statically referenced local temporary was not promoted to the `Global` root in `place_root_key`. This does not affect the normal process, but will directly degrade all static locks to local root. I'll also take a look to see if `LocalDecl` has a ready-made static reference interface.

    pub fn is_ref_for_guard(&self) -> bool {
        matches!(self.local_info(), LocalInfo::User(BindingForm::RefForGuard(_)))
    }

    /// Returns `Some` if this is a reference to a static item that is used to
    /// access that static.
    pub fn is_ref_to_static(&self) -> bool {
        matches!(self.local_info(), LocalInfo::StaticRef { .. })
    }

    /// Returns `Some` if this is a reference to a thread-local static item that is used to
    /// access that static.
    pub fn is_ref_to_thread_local(&self) -> bool {
        match self.local_info() {
            LocalInfo::StaticRef { is_thread_local, .. } => *is_thread_local,
            _ => false,
        }
    }

    current_def_id: DefId,

                body,
                state,
                source.local,

#### Assistant · final_answer · 2026-03-25 04:09:42 UTC

Refactoring completed.`tools/lockdep/analysis` now no longer piles most of the logic in one file:
- Top-level orchestration remains in [collect.rs](/root/asterinas-codex/tools/lockdep/analysis/src/collect.rs)
- IRQ context and entry identification are split into [context.rs](/root/asterinas-codex/tools/lockdep/analysis/src/collect/context.rs)- MIR status advancement and call/effect processing are split to [mir.rs](/root/asterinas-codex/tools/lockdep/analysis/src/collect/mir.rs)
- lock class, place/origin, callback analysis is split into [place.rs](/root/asterinas-codex/tools/lockdep/analysis/src/collect/place.rs)- Cross-function summary, usage merging, and edge normalization are split into [summary.rs](/root/asterinas-codex/tools/lockdep/analysis/src/collect/summary.rs)The test side has also been disassembled, and it is no longer a long test function. Now [fixture_cases.rs](/root/asterinas-codex/tools/lockdep/tests/fixture_cases.rs) is split into 6 independent `#[test]` according to the theme, and a shared fixture is used to cache and reuse the analysis results, making the logic clearer.The returned-guard case for the fixture itself remains in [lib.rs](/root/asterinas-codex/tools/lockdep/tests/fixtures/ostd-lockdep-cases/src/lib.rs).验证已完成：
- `cargo build --manifest-path tools/lockdep/Cargo.toml`
- `cargo test --manifest-path tools/lockdep/Cargo.toml --test fixture_cases`
- `cargo run --manifest-path tools/lockdep/Cargo.toml -- -p aster-kernel --target x86_64-unknown-none -- --quiet`The results of `aster-kernel` remain at 2489 lock events and 807 lock edges, which are the same as before reconstruction.  
If you want, I can continue to submit this refactoring as a commit.
